data-framerate="30"/&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;\'><img alt="File:Voyager Captures Sounds of Interstellar Space.webm" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Voyager_Captures_Sounds_of_Interstellar_Space.webm/220px--Voyager_Captures_Sounds_of_Interstellar_Space.webm.jpg" style="width:220px;height:124px"/><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3c/Voyager_Captures_Sounds_of_Interstellar_Space.webm" target="new" title="Play media"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Voyager_Captures_Sounds_of_Interstellar_Space.webm" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Voyager 1</i> transmitted audio signals generated by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plasma_waves" title="Plasma waves">plasma waves</a> from interstellar space</div></div></div>\n<p>On September 12, 2013, NASA officially confirmed that <i>Voyager 1</i> had reached the <a href="/wiki/Interstellar_medium" title="Interstellar medium">interstellar medium</a> in August 2012 as previously observed, with a generally accepted date of August 25, 2012 (~10d short of 34yrs since launch), the date durable changes in the density of energetic particles were first detected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cowen2013_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cowen2013-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kerr2013_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kerr2013-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gurnett2013_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gurnett2013-64">[64]</a></sup> By this point most space scientists had abandoned the hypothesis that a change in magnetic field direction must accompany crossing of the heliopause;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kerr2013_63-2"><a href="#cite_note-Kerr2013-63">[63]</a></sup> a new model of the heliopause predicted that no such change would be found.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Swisdak2013_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Swisdak2013-74">[74]</a></sup> A key finding that persuaded many scientists that the heliopause had been crossed was an indirect measurement of an 80-fold increase in electron density, based on the frequency of <a href="/wiki/Waves_in_plasmas" title="Waves in plasmas">plasma oscillations</a> observed beginning on April 9, 2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kerr2013_63-3"><a href="#cite_note-Kerr2013-63">[63]</a></sup> triggered by a <a href="/wiki/Coronal_mass_ejection" title="Coronal mass ejection">solar outburst</a> that had occurred in March 2012<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cook2013_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cook2013-60">[60]</a></sup> (electron density is expected to be two orders of magnitude higher outside the heliopause than within).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cowen2013_62-2"><a href="#cite_note-Cowen2013-62">[62]</a></sup> Weaker sets of oscillations measured in October and November 2012<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-How_We_Know_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-How_We_Know-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morin2013_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morin2013-75">[75]</a></sup> provided additional data. An indirect measurement was required because <i>Voyager 1</i>\'s plasma spectrometer had stopped working in 1980.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gurnett2013_64-2"><a href="#cite_note-Gurnett2013-64">[64]</a></sup> In September 2013, NASA released recordings of audio <a href="/wiki/Transducer" title="Transducer">transductions</a> of these plasma waves, the first to be measured in interstellar space.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-space.22777_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-space.22777-76">[76]</a></sup>\n</p><p>While <i>Voyager 1</i> is commonly spoken of as having left the Solar System simultaneously with having left the heliosphere, the two are not the same. The Solar System is usually defined as the vastly larger region of space populated by bodies that orbit the Sun. The craft is presently less than one-seventh the distance to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aphelion" title="Aphelion">aphelion</a> of <a href="/wiki/90377_Sedna" title="90377 Sedna">Sedna</a>, and it has not yet entered the <a href="/wiki/Oort_cloud" title="Oort cloud">Oort cloud</a>, the source region of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Long-period_comet" title="Long-period comet">long-period comets</a>, regarded by astronomers as the outermost zone of the Solar System.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ghose2013_61-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ghose2013-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-How_We_Know_72-2"><a href="#cite_note-How_We_Know-72">[72]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_of_the_probe">Future of the probe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Voyager_1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Future of the probe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Voyager_1_Radio_Signal_21_Feb_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Voyager_1_Radio_Signal_21_Feb_2013.jpg/170px-Voyager_1_Radio_Signal_21_Feb_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Voyager_1_Radio_Signal_21_Feb_2013.jpg/255px-Voyager_1_Radio_Signal_21_Feb_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Voyager_1_Radio_Signal_21_Feb_2013.jpg/340px-Voyager_1_Radio_Signal_21_Feb_2013.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Voyager_1_Radio_Signal_21_Feb_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Image of <i>Voyager 1</i>\'s radio signal on February 21, 2013<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VoyagerOne_Aug_2_2018.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="1232" data-file-width="2468" decoding="async" height="100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/VoyagerOne_Aug_2_2018.png/200px-VoyagerOne_Aug_2_2018.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/VoyagerOne_Aug_2_2018.png/300px-VoyagerOne_Aug_2_2018.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/VoyagerOne_Aug_2_2018.png/400px-VoyagerOne_Aug_2_2018.png 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Simulated view of <i>Voyager 1</i> relative to the Solar System on August 2, 2018.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Voyagerprobes_Aug_2_2018.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="1249" data-file-width="3044" decoding="async" height="82" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Voyagerprobes_Aug_2_2018.png/200px-Voyagerprobes_Aug_2_2018.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Voyagerprobes_Aug_2_2018.png/300px-Voyagerprobes_Aug_2_2018.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Voyagerprobes_Aug_2_2018.png/400px-Voyagerprobes_Aug_2_2018.png 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Simulated view of the Voyager probes relative to the Solar System and heliopause on August 2, 2018.</div></div></div></div>\n<p><i>Voyager 1</i> is expected to reach the theorized <a href="/wiki/Oort_cloud" title="Oort cloud">Oort cloud</a> in about 300 years<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jpl.PIA17046_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-jpl.PIA17046-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ut.104717_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-ut.104717-79">[79]</a></sup> and take about 30,000 years to pass through it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ghose2013_61-3"><a href="#cite_note-Ghose2013-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-How_We_Know_72-3"><a href="#cite_note-How_We_Know-72">[72]</a></sup> Though it is not heading towards any particular star, in about <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_far_future#Spacecraft_and_space_exploration" title="Timeline of the far future">40,000 years</a>, it will pass within 1.6 <a href="/wiki/Light-year" title="Light-year">light-years</a> of the star <a href="/wiki/Gliese_445" title="Gliese 445">Gliese 445</a>, which is at present in the <a href="/wiki/Constellation" title="Constellation">constellation</a> <a href="/wiki/Camelopardalis" title="Camelopardalis">Camelopardalis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-voyager_interstellar_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-voyager_interstellar-80">[80]</a></sup> That star is generally moving towards the <a href="/wiki/Solar_System" title="Solar System">Solar System</a> at about 119&#160;km/s (430,000&#160;km/h; 270,000&#160;mph).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-voyager_interstellar_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-voyager_interstellar-80">[80]</a></sup> NASA says that "The <i>Voyagers</i> are destined&#8212;perhaps eternally&#8212;to wander the Milky Way."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Provided <i>Voyager 1</i> does not collide with anything and is not retrieved, the <i><a href="/wiki/New_Horizons" title="New Horizons">New Horizons</a></i> space probe will never pass it, despite being launched from Earth at a faster speed than either Voyager spacecraft.  The Voyager spacecraft benefited from multiple planetary flybys to increase their heliocentric velocities, whereas <i>New Horizons</i> received only a single such boost, from its Jupiter flyby. As of 2018, <i>New Horizons</i> is traveling at about 14 km/s, 3 km/s slower than <i>Voyager 1</i>, and is still slowing down.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Horizons2006_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-New_Horizons2006-82">[82]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2017 it was announced that NASA had successfully fired up all four of <i>Voyager 1</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'</span>s trajectory correction maneuver (TCM) thrusters. The TCM thrusters will be used in the place of a degraded set of jets which were used to help keep the probe\'s antenna pointed towards the Earth.  Use of the TCM thrusters will allow <i>Voyager 1</i> to continue to transmit data to NASA for two to three more years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Year</th>\n<th>End of specific capabilities as a result of the available electrical power limitations<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2007</td>\n<td>Termination of plasma subsystem (PLS)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2008</td>\n<td>Power off Planetary Radio Astronomy Experiment (PRA)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2016<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></td>\n<td>Termination of scan platform and Ultraviolet Spectrometer (UVS) observations\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2018 approx.</td>\n<td>Termination of Data Tape Recorder (DTR) operations (limited by ability to capture 1.4&#160;kbit/s data using a 70&#160;m/34&#160;m antenna array; this is the minimum rate at which the DTR can read out data)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2019&#8211;2020 approx.</td>\n<td>Termination of <a href="/wiki/Gyroscope" title="Gyroscope">gyroscopic</a> operations (previously 2017, but backup thrusters active for continuation of gyroscopic operations.)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2020</td>\n<td>Start shutdown of science instruments (as of  October&#160;18, 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Voyager_1&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the order is undecided, however the Low-Energy Charged Particles, Cosmic Ray Subsystem, Magnetometer, and Plasma Wave Subsystem instruments are expected to still be operating)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA2010.10.18_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA2010.10.18-87">[87]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2025&#8211;2030</td>\n<td>Will no longer be able to power even a single instrument.\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Golden_record">Golden record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Voyager_1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Golden record">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio class="kskin" controls="" data-durationhint="4.26525" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Voyager_Golden_Record_greeting_in_English.ogg" data-startoffset="0" id="mwe_player_4" preload="none" style="width:220px"><source data-bandwidth="27999" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (28 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6f/Voyager_Golden_Record_greeting_in_English.ogg" type=\'audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"\'/><source data-bandwidth="76368" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-title="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/6/6f/Voyager_Golden_Record_greeting_in_English.ogg/Voyager_Golden_Record_greeting_in_English.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg"/></audio></div> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Voyager_Golden_Record_greeting_in_English.ogg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A child\'s greeting in English recorded on the <a href="/wiki/Voyager_Golden_Record" title="Voyager Golden Record">Voyager Golden Record</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Sounds_of_Earth_-_GPN-2000-001976.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2999" data-file-width="2389" decoding="async" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/The_Sounds_of_Earth_-_GPN-2000-001976.jpg/100px-The_Sounds_of_Earth_-_GPN-2000-001976.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/The_Sounds_of_Earth_-_GPN-2000-001976.jpg/150px-The_Sounds_of_Earth_-_GPN-2000-001976.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/The_Sounds_of_Earth_-_GPN-2000-001976.jpg/201px-The_Sounds_of_Earth_-_GPN-2000-001976.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Sounds_of_Earth_-_GPN-2000-001976.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><center><i>Voyager</i> Golden Record</center></div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Voyager_Golden_Record" title="Voyager Golden Record">Voyager Golden Record</a></div>\n<p>Each Voyager space probe carries a gold-plated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gramophone_record" title="Gramophone record">audio-visual disc</a>, should the spacecraft ever be found by intelligent life forms from other planetary systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ferris-201205_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ferris-201205-88">[88]</a></sup> The disc carries photos of the <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a> and its lifeforms, a range of scientific information, spoken greetings from people such as the <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">Secretary-General of the United Nations</a> and the President of the United States and a medley, "Sounds of Earth," that includes the sounds of whales, a baby crying, waves breaking on a shore, and a collection of music including works by <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blind_Willie_Johnson" title="Blind Willie Johnson">Blind Willie Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Berry" title="Chuck Berry">Chuck Berry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Valya_Balkanska" title="Valya Balkanska">Valya Balkanska</a>. Other Eastern and Western classics are included, as well as various performances of indigenous music from around the world. The record also contains greetings in 55 different languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa.gold_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-nasa.gold-89">[89]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Voyager_1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0a/Interstellar_probes_trajectory.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="375" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Interstellar_probes_trajectory.svg/250px-Interstellar_probes_trajectory.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Interstellar_probes_trajectory.svg/375px-Interstellar_probes_trajectory.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Interstellar_probes_trajectory.svg/500px-Interstellar_probes_trajectory.svg.png 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Interstellar_probes_trajectory.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ecliptic_coordinate_system#Spherical_coordinates" title="Ecliptic coordinate system">Heliocentric positions</a> of the five <a href="/wiki/Interstellar_probe" title="Interstellar probe">interstellar probes</a> (squares) and other bodies (circles) until 2020, with launch and flyby dates. Markers denote positions on <span class="nowrap">1 January</span> of each year, with every fifth year labelled.<br style="margin-bottom:1ex;"/><span class="nowrap">Plot 1</span> is viewed from the <a href="/wiki/Orbital_pole#Ecliptic_pole" title="Orbital pole">north ecliptic pole</a>, to scale; <span class="nowrap">plots 2 to 4</span> are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third-angle_projection" title="Third-angle projection">third-angle projections</a> at 20% scale.<br style="margin-bottom:1ex;"/>In <a class="external text" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0a/Interstellar_probes_trajectory.svg"><span class="nowrap">the SVG file,</span></a> hover over a trajectory or orbit to highlight it and its associated launches and flybys.</div></div></div>\n<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul
